<gmap_id>0x808f80b041d3d1fb:0x6a25f3d54b96b434< /gmap_id><review>Like others before me, again just stating facts here so that others can make informed decisions before renting from Domain. I'll list my positives and negatives and let you make your own informed decisions.

DO read all of the reviews online, as I thought when we rented here that people must have been crazy, on the surface this place looks amazing, but know that a lot of what other people are writing are very true. So I will just leave you with my own experiences.

1.) Location - The location of the building is close to downtown Oakland. At first it was great, walking distance to Bart, restaurants etc. However at night its another story. You are one block from a freeway, and West Oakland, a few blocks from a major police station, and near so many government buildings that attract homeless, transients, and deadbeats. I can't tell you how many times I saw flashing police lights, sirens from fire trucks, hookers on the street corner, along with people yelling and screaming from the street below. I was on the 6th floor, and nose echo's up the building.

2.) The fire alarms - I thought there was no way that could be an issue still a year before that someone had posted before I moved in. Oh its still an issue, and be ready to go downstairs at 3,4,5 in the morning to the street level. Oh and if its not this building that wakes you up, then it will be the even worse one across the street, as they have issues to.

3.) The elevators. Get used to walking the stairs. Great for exercise, but honestly I could tell you how many times that they actually worked. The issue with the building is that construction started in 2007/8 and then stopped due to the financial crisis. The building was left open and unfinished, and thus with rust and rain it has wrecked havoc on the building systems ever since, on top of that the two elevators on D block are interior elevators but in an exterior setting. They will never work properly.

4.) Security. This one definitely goes with number 1. Security is pretty much a joke here. The cameras don't capture any footage, cars wait at the garage doors to follow people in to either park for free, or steal what they can, doors are propped open or people wait by the entries to sneak in as someone leaves. I had my bicycle tire stolen from a locked bike in a locked bike room in the basement. I myself had to alert the team that the door had been broken once, the next time I went down the door was completely open and bingo my tire gone. Oh and insurance won't cover it, so basically don't leave anything anywhere unless its in your locked apartment and even then its probably not safe.

5.) Packages. Don't expect amazon to deliver your packages. If they can't get in the building, they will leave it in the alley by the front door. If you order one of those food boxes, outside on the front door feeding the homeless. Instacart may make it to the lobby, but even then I saw it sitting there for 24-48hours rotting. My wife lost so many items that never made it into their "secure lockers" people don't pick up their packages, so the lockers are full, and then sometimes items make it into the mail room, but again only if someone leaves the door open - great security.

6.) Pets and cleanliness - Not sure why pet owners with dogs can't clean up after their pet has an accident and pees in the elevator or poos on the floor, but somehow the place remains a mess.

Better stuff.
1.) B block is probably the best being in the middle, but then you are look at neighbors on either side. Units on the end seem like they are the bomb, views of the sunset, off a quiet alley, exterior wrap around balconies.
2.) The roof top BBQ grill works very well, and the amenity is great.
3.) The gym has some amazing equipment. When/If it reopens
4.) Lots of open parking, never had an issue finding a space, and if you don't live in the building you can park for free too, just follow someone in. :)
5.) Staff was pretty helpful most of the time. If you caught them on a good day, they were happy to help.<//review>< Pictures>
None<//Pictures>

<userid>117141667952789867652<//userid><Time>1603484315734</Time><Text>My partner and I just moved here in August.

App/movein process:
Easy. Simple. Did everything online in a single day.

Office staff:
I toured with Julia, Asst Mgr. She was very accommodating (I'm also a property mgr so I know I can be a bit difficult), friendly, and helpful.

Tahlia helped with the app process. Super friendly, she was new but said it straight up which is always smart, and definitely helpful.

Desmond, I barely worked with but was certainly polite and helpful the few times we did communicate.

Mgr is Brittany, I had an issue while moving, unrelated to Domain, and she was both helpful and supportive even though she'd never met me before.

The unit: I have a 795 sqft 1bed which I LOVE. The bedroom is a bit small, so if you've got a king don't expect sidetables. Fits a queen and 2 sidetables with a little extra space. Lg bathroom with 2 doors, we covered the door to bedroom w/ shelving. Kitchen is open which I love, we just purchased an island. Built in desk in the corner makes my day every time I use it. Not a lot of lighting, you'll need plenty of lamps.

Parking: Great price, always good spots available. My last place was $270 but much cheaper rent. To be clear to mgmt: I would not have moved here if parking was any more expensive so I wouldn't suggest increasing.

Utilities: I haven't received yet. A bit worried about the rates considering some of the other posts, so we'll see..

Property: The 2 courtyards w/ bbqs and firepits are amazing. One day we'll get to use the rooftop and gym as well, not their fault. Yes, sometimes there is dog pee on the concrete - not mgmt fault. It's unrealistic to expect power washing daily. More realistically -- residents with pets (such as myself) need to monitor their animals and prevent peeing inside the property. They provide bags at exits which is appreciated.

Location: YAS.. althought for now a lowercase yas due to Covid, but there's still bars and restaurants who've opened up with outdoor seating. Bart 2 blocks away, Flax Art Supply 2 blocks away, not as close to a grocery store as I'd like but a short drive.<//Text></record></dataset><record>

If I could give this place 10 stars I would!

<text>Out of an hour long class they frequently spend 40 minutes on solo work. During this time the only instruction is watching the instructor dance in the front of the room. If you do not get what the instructor is doing you will not be corrected or have an opportunity to ask a question. The music just keeps going and you just have to try again when the instructor repeats the movement.

Then they switch to partner work. The partner work instruction is adequate in quality, but the remaining 20 minutes is insufficient to fully grasp the partner sequence.

Ultimately there is very little correction if you are doing something wrong.

This is better than some studios, but no where near as good as a studio can be. They do not deserve the 1 star rating I‚Äôm giving them, but they also do not deserve the 5 star rating they have maintained. If their overall rating was 4 stars I think that would more accurately reflect the studio.

My suggestion for improvement would be to either place the solo work in a separate class or to reduce the amount of curriculum covered in a class so that it can be done properly.<//text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMue1ak75p6FKbtfwYwuSwuMgXP6U1j3qZ_F4Zr=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pics>< Resp>

< Review>
David and his crew at Majesty in Motion are absolutely phenomenal!
My fianc√© and I decided to try out salsa dancing on a whim last January and ended up at Tango Del Rey on a Friday evening. The first hour of the night was a class hosted by David and that was our first exposure to salsa. Needless to say, we had a great time and began taking classes at the studio soon after.

Since then, I have danced in Mexico, Peru, Boston, and NY and NONE of the classes I have taken can compare to our experience at Majesty in Motion. David and his instructors are not only great dancers themselves, but they are one with the dance. As instructors, they understand the physical and mental blocks of their students better than the students themselves and this is the defining characteristic of great teachers and the single most important quality that has allowed us to progress as well as we have with this dance company.

Joining the salsa team has positively impacted my life in ways I could have never imagined. Never having danced before in my entire life, it's an honor to be a part of a team comprised of such motivating, talented, and charismatic individuals.

To be honest, the thought of learning how to dance first terrified me. Letting the music move you is easier said than done.I was terrified that I would never be good enough. I didn‚Äôt know how to dance. I thought I would "fail". So I held on tighter, tensed up, got stiff.

David and Jennifer have taught me that the music‚Äôs always playing. We just have to decide if we‚Äôre still going to hold ourselves back, or if we‚Äôre going to dance. Try it yourself. Let go of those reigns. Give in. Surrender. Feel the music. Feel the rhythm. And then, when you‚Äôre ready, let it carry you. Let it move you.

We look forward to dancing around the world, but we'll always find ourselves back at Majesty!</Review>
